  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8ea0512c-da3b-4841-ae7a-123179bbaf1b'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1562698597595131931"><b>Yuda</b>, "si iblis", seorang pemanjat tebing dan petaruh yang melecehkan nilai-nilai masyarakat. <b>Parang Jati</b>, "si malaikat", seorang pemuda berjari duabelas yang dibentuk oleh ayah angkatnya untuk menanggung duka dunia. <b>Marja</b>, "si manusia", seorang gadis bertubuh kuda feji dan berjiwa matahari.<br/><br/>Mereka terlibat dalam segitiga cinta yang lembut, di antara pengalaman-pengalaman k</span>
  <span id="freeText1562698597595131931" style="display:none"><b>Yuda</b>, "si iblis", seorang pemanjat tebing dan petaruh yang melecehkan nilai-nilai masyarakat. <b>Parang Jati</b>, "si malaikat", seorang pemuda berjari duabelas yang dibentuk oleh ayah angkatnya untuk menanggung duka dunia. <b>Marja</b>, "si manusia", seorang gadis bertubuh kuda feji dan berjiwa matahari.<br /><br />Mereka terlibat dalam segitiga cinta yang lembut, di antara pengalaman-pengalaman keras yang berawal dari sebuah kejadian aneh-- orang mati yang bangkit dari kubur-- menuju penyelamatan perbukitan gamping di selatan Jawa.<br />Di antara semua itu, Bilangan Fu sayup-sayup menyingkapkan diri.<br /><br /><br />Pengarang menamai nafas novelnya "spiritualisme kritis". Yaitu, yang mengangkat wacana spiritual-- keagamaan, kebatinan, maupun mistik-- ke dalam kerangka yang menghormatinya sekaligus bersikap kritis kepadanya, yang mengangkat wacana keberimanan, tanpa terjebak dalam dakwah hitam dan putih.<br /><br />Novel ini adalah manifesto Ayu Utami tentang sebuah sikap yang dianggap perlu diutamakan di zaman ini: sikap religius ataupun spiritual, yang kritis.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1562698597595131931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_35025628" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35025628" />
    <a title="Anang Kurniawan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1179025-anang-kurniawan"><img alt="Anang Kurniawan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/35025628?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anang Kurniawan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anang Kurniawan" href="/user/show/1179025-anang-kurniawan">Anang Kurniawan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer35025628" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2832471920394617011">This week, the court for Habieb Rizieq was held on the accusation of provoking group of mass attacking their ‘enemies.’ Still well-remembered, two groups of people, two different beliefs, two truth of self-assumption, were confronting each to each, they say, attempting to erect the truth. Truth? For whom? The mentioned-case is an notable example of how easy to fertilize hatred to the outsiders of certain ‘non-believers.’ Pluralism, even Islam recognizes the fact, is no longer, for this nation-In</span>
  <span id="freeText2832471920394617011" style="display:none">This week, the court for Habieb Rizieq was held on the accusation of provoking group of mass attacking their ‘enemies.’ Still well-remembered, two groups of people, two different beliefs, two truth of self-assumption, were confronting each to each, they say, attempting to erect the truth. Truth? For whom? The mentioned-case is an notable example of how easy to fertilize hatred to the outsiders of certain ‘non-believers.’ Pluralism, even Islam recognizes the fact, is no longer, for this nation-Indonesia, a potency to leverage the prestige, or, even the welfare. Pluralism is nothing but tool: tool to power. On-the-name-of-religion conflicts are common here, and, now.<br /><br />Self-truth: which is just self-assumption, is prominent and visible threat for this post-modernism. Self-truth tends to negates others. It is the problem of how to set the viewpoint in order to see and judge everything in proper manners.<br /><br />One proposal comes fro Ayu Utami, launching her new novel, Bilangan Fu. Concerns to the above case, she comments through the novel: the needs of critical spiritualism. It needs to develop the act to critic (laku kritik) in a framework of respecting each to each without being trapped to any black-and-white dogmatic preach.<br /><br />The novel comprises three major issues: modernism, monotheism, and militarism. All, she said, are the major antagonist to perform the act of post-modernism. The novel utilizes the setting of climbing activities in Watugunung, described as a place attempting to defend itself from the attack of modernism. Ayu Utami, still, creates her characters beautifully elaborated, equipped with her technique of polyphonic. She employs all: narrative and news article and journal and interior monologue. What makes this novel amazing is the fact that she must perform huge research before composing the story. She grasps the traditional myths and Bible and puppet (wayang).<br /><br />Yuda, her major characters, represents an idea of modern that views everything from modernistic viewpoint: rationalism and capitalism. The language he knows is bet (p.6). he doubts everything: social values and myth and others. He is ‘the devil.’ However, this character is the opening gate for another character to show: Parangjati. He is ‘the angel’: the preacher. Yuda doubts and questions, Parangjati answers.<br /><br />The first section, Modernism, is the confrontation of rational viewpoint and act to traditional life’s way and myth. The preacher: Parangjati, has these:<br />1. Superstitious is considered wrong due to the emergence of modern thinking, though modern thinking cannot fully free from it.<br />2. People freed from superstitious, through modern thinking, are those who gain benefits: the capitalist.<br />3. Modernism is private intended tools to utilize superstitious.<br />4. Superstitious, indeed, is required.<br /><br />Critique to monotheism is becoming the central point of the second section. It criticizes the Semitic religion: monotheism, as those who frequently involved in the conflicts. Parangjati compares concepts of god in monotheism to those in eastern religion in order to figure out the grass root of the tendency. Parangjati says that the concept of one-ness in monotheism tends to negate others. God comes in negation. It differs in eastern religions, recognizing the concept of shunya (zero) in god. This, he concludes, creates an atmosphere that can accept outsiders as shunya is able to be everywhere. Of course, the faults are in the bearers.<br /><br />Parangjati yells the needs of considering the ancient tradition: the rites and the myth and beliefs, to maintain the order of life. Earth, he says, is not solely provided for human, but, other creatures: the visible and the invincible.<br /><br />‘The only thing to manifest today is goodness; truth must be held high, and not to touch the Earth, not manifest today. For, if truth manifest today, it is nothing but power (p. 408).’<br /><br />The third, Militarism, is his conclusion and emphasis to the enemies of post-modernism. Modernism, monotheism, and militarism are tools only for those attempting to gain self-benefit.<br /><br />‘The people of post-modern are behaving act to critic. No longer they tend and behave anti to attempt the liberation of others from the dark. Act to critic is awareness that truth is everywhere and, behind dark shadow of the will to power. What we can do is to criticize the power persistently: not to ruin it, but to balance. In this case, monotheism needs to learn from eastern religion, that does not view people between the war of God vs. devil, but as the act of equalizer.<br /><br />Outward, act to critic represents the balancer of over powers. Inward, act to critic hold high self-truth. Truth is mystery, if down-to-earth, will manifest to laws: pipe and infuse pumping hallow breath.<br /><br />For self, act to critic hold the mystery of truth and laws, higher than surface, so that good and peace may develop naturally on earth.’ (pp. 470-80)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2832471920394617011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3630269789">

<div id="review_1358066845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1358066845" />
    <a title="Jan-Joost Bouwman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532911-jan-joost-bouwman"><img alt="Jan-Joost Bouwman" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1358066845?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan-Joost Bouwman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan-Joost Bouwman" href="/user/show/32532911-jan-joost-bouwman">Jan-Joost Bouwman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1358066845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6872882106359322800">I have to admit I probably would never have picked this book if it hadn't been in the Oxfam Novib book club series a couple of years aho. It didn't appeal very much to me from the cover text. Two rock climbers, one of whom sees supernatural things? I have very little interest in either subject. I think mountaineers have a death wish and rockclimbers are even worst. I am very unspiritual and don't usually have a lot of patience for it. Still, this book was a pleasant surprise.<br/><br/>At the core is the s</span>
  <span id="freeText6872882106359322800" style="display:none">I have to admit I probably would never have picked this book if it hadn't been in the Oxfam Novib book club series a couple of years aho. It didn't appeal very much to me from the cover text. Two rock climbers, one of whom sees supernatural things? I have very little interest in either subject. I think mountaineers have a death wish and rockclimbers are even worst. I am very unspiritual and don't usually have a lot of patience for it. Still, this book was a pleasant surprise.<br /><br />At the core is the story of a special friendship, with sexual undertones, between city boy Yuda and country boy Jati. Yuda likes to go rockclimbing in Jati's native area. Jati is everything he is not, quiet, spiritual, considerate of other peoples feeling, interested in literature and folk history and religion, passionate about preserving the environment and the karst hills before they are mined for their chalk. Yuda doesn't understand Jati's interests and passions, but takes an instant liking to him. And after a silly bet they start clean climbing together.<br />Jati comes from a spiritual background and the whole area seems full of mysterious creatures and entities. The local people have held these in respect, but recently greed under the cover of pure Islam has led to conflicts. Conflicts fuelled by the struggle between Police and Military after the resignation of the dictator Suharto. Jati's attempts to protect the hills brings him in the frontline of this conflict, against his younger brother. The brother that grew up in much poorer circumstances and has chosen for religious zealotism as a way out of poverty.<br /><br />The story is quite exciting, even though you know it is not ending well. At times the filosofical bits are a bit of a drag (especially the "news paper clippings"). But the friendship, the sexual tension of the triangle between the two boys and Yuda's girlfriend, combined with the mystery of missing corpses and mysterious assisins make up for that. It is also a fascinating insight into a world I know so little about, even with the connection we have with Indonesia as a former colony.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6872882106359322800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The first is Yuda, a modern-thinking climber who make friends with Parang Jati, a geology student from ITB who's in a mission to learn climbing technique from Yuda.<br/><br/>At first, the very different personalities make Yuda feels discomfort with Parang Jati.   <span id="freeText6785844328328469509" style="display:none">So far I've managed to finish half of the book. Bilangan Fu is a type of book that inspires as well as surprises me. I might not say it entertains but it's quite interesting to follow.<br /><br />There are two main charachters in this book. The first is Yuda, a modern-thinking climber who make friends with Parang Jati, a geology student from ITB who's in a mission to learn climbing technique from Yuda.<br /><br />At first, the very different personalities make Yuda feels discomfort with Parang Jati. Yuda embraces logical thinking while Parang Jati is a bright scholar who still preserve traditional values. But eventually yuda thinks that his new friend is not as bad as he tought.<br /><br />Bilangan Fu is not only a story about friendship or competition. It's a critical statement of history, traditional values and personalities that wrapped in mundane conflicts. </span>

<div id="review_33887426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33887426" />
    <a title="Tetrin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/813917-tetrin"><img alt="Tetrin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1222510706p2/813917.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33887426?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tetrin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tetrin" href="/user/show/813917-tetrin">Tetrin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33887426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17421990858510296393">This books emphasize what differences in modernism, monotheism, and militarism. Modernism, reflected in one character, named Yudha, sceptic, rationalist, and capitalist. Monotheism is described by Parang jati, who tells us that all the form of monotheism can't save our forest, air, water, mountain from exploitation and violance, like the traditionalism did well. The last one, militarism wrap everything depends on it needs. It opens my eyes that all events previously happened in my life, murder o</span>
  <span id="freeText17421990858510296393" style="display:none">This books emphasize what differences in modernism, monotheism, and militarism. //<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2D6rjj6KXxtxFGIpIBkJP80EcI21u0gY0C1hAjeKxfE1KRm0r0Wd0IRZ+GEFjcXAqZRIdVt69KuBuqwI7bpHwQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JIq+zzWwlSgNDu//KFYAGN4f1o9DXf+FQdIWugdMmqbJnQz1pH9X4/hDdbcNwsznuo/ud62cQzYQRduw3XwYlg==')})
  }
//]]>

Pada saat yang sama, Dimas menerima k<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText12989382622878399208\" style=\"display:none\">Paris, Mei 1968. \n\nKetika revolusi mahasiswa berkecamuk di Paris, Dimas Suryo seorang eksil politik Indonesia bertemu Vivienne Deveraux, seorang mahasiswa Prancis yang ikut demonstrasi melawan pemerintah Prancis. Pada saat yang sama, Dimas menerima kabar dari Jakarta: Hananto Prawiro, sahabatnya, ditangkap tentara dan dinyatakan tewas. Dimas merasa cemas dan gamang. Bersama puluhan wartawan dan seniman lain, dia tak bisa kembali ke Jakarta karena paspornya dicabut oleh pemerintah Indonesia. Sejak itu mereka mengelana tanpa status yang jelas dari Santiago ke Havana, ke Peking dan akhirnya mendarat di tanah Eropa untuk mendapatkan suaka dan menetap di sana.\n\nDi tengah kesibukan mengelola Restoran Tanah Air di Paris bersama tiga kawannya: Nug, Tjai, dan Risjaf—mereka berempat disebut Empat Pilar Tanah Air—Dimas, terus-menerus dikejar rasa bersalah karena kawan-kawannya di Indonesia satu persatu tumbang, dikejar, ditembak, atau menghilang begitu saja dalam perburuan Peristiwa 30 September. Bagi pedukuhan yang kecil, miskin, terpencil dan bersahaja itu, ronggeng adalah perlambang. Tanpanya dukuh itu merasakah kehilangan jati diri.\n\nDengan segera Srintil menjadi tokoh yang amat terkenal dan digandrungi. Cantik dan menggoda. Semua ingin pernah bersama ronggeng itu. Dari kaula biasa hingga pekabat-pejabat desa maupun kabupaten. \n\nNamun malapetaka politik tahun 1965 membuat dukuh tersebut hancur, baik secara fisik maupun mental. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16632672372301935290">Justina Ayu Utami atau hanya Ayu Utami (lahir di Bogor, Jawa Barat, 21 November 1968) adalah aktivis jurnalis dan novelis Indonesia, ia besar di Jakarta dan menamatkan kuliah di Fakultas Sastra Universitas Indonesia.<br/>Ia pernah menjadi wartawan di majalah Humor, Matra, Forum Keadilan, dan D&R. Tak lama setelah penutupan Tempo, Editor dan Detik pada masa Orde Baru, ia ikut mendirikan Aliansi Jurnalis</span>
  <span id="freeText16632672372301935290" style="display:none">Justina Ayu Utami atau hanya Ayu Utami (lahir di Bogor, Jawa Barat, 21 November 1968) adalah aktivis jurnalis dan novelis Indonesia, ia besar di Jakarta dan menamatkan kuliah di Fakultas Sastra Universitas Indonesia.<br />Ia pernah menjadi wartawan di majalah Humor, Matra, Forum Keadilan, dan D&amp;R. Tak lama setelah penutupan Tempo, Editor dan Detik pada masa Orde Baru, ia ikut mendirikan Aliansi Jurnalis Independen yang memprotes pembredelan. Kini ia bekerja di jurnal kebudayaan Kalam dan di Teater Utan Kayu. Novelnya yang pertama, Saman, mendapatkan sambutan dari berbagai kritikus dan dianggap memberikan warna baru dalam sastra Indonesia.<br /><br />Ayu dikenal sebagai novelis sejak novelnya Saman memenangi sayembara penulisan roman Dewan Kesenian Jakarta 1998. Dalam waktu tiga tahun Saman terjual 55 ribu eksemplar. Berkat Saman pula, Ayu mendapat Prince Claus Award 2000 dari Prince Claus Fund, sebuah yayasan yang bermarkas di Den Haag, yang mempunyai misi mendukung dan memajukan kegiatan di bidang budaya dan pembangunan. Akhir 2001, ia meluncurkan novel Larung.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16632672372301935290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
